Women's Special

How to Be a Female Office Worker

— Mei Ting

In recent years, the number of women working in society has gradually increased. However, at the same time, disreputable titles and embarrassing [situations] have become increasingly common. On the one hand, this is due to society's underestimation of women and the habit of making a fuss about minor things. On the other hand, it is brought about by the women themselves who work in society. I believe that a woman squeezing into today's society—a male-centered society—and snatching a rice bowl from their hands is not something to be proud of, but rather something to be regarded as simply lucky. We are the lucky ones who have gained a self-reliant position. How should we conduct ourselves? This is a personal question worth discussing.

The reason why female office workers are criticized by society is that there are certainly unsatisfactory aspects. Apart from the unavoidable disadvantage due to physiological reasons compared to men, I believe that since men and women are equal and receive the same salary, you should use your ability to do your duty and work equally with your colleagues. This is an absolute rule that female office workers should abide by. As for disreputable actions caused by other personnel matters within the scope of work, they should also be absolutely avoided. Then the nickname "vase" will naturally not be put on your heads.

At the same time, female office workers also have a very common bad habit, which is "arriving late and leaving early." Although this cannot be generalized, the fact tells us that in offices where attendance check-in is only considered a formality and is not strictly enforced, female office workers' late arrivals and early departures have become very common and ought to be conservative and thrifty (although there are exceptions where heavy makeup is necessary due to business reasons). If you want to win the favor of colleagues or the company's managers with your own beauty, it is tantamount to selling your own body, fundamentally losing the task and mission of the female office worker herself. This is the biggest reason why one is most easily looked down upon.

As for disreputable actions caused by other personnel matters within the scope of work, they should also be absolutely avoided. There are certainly many so-called other personnel matters, such as colleagues falling in love, etc., which are sufficient to affect personal reputation. Although love is something that cannot be abandoned in life, we should recognize that love is a kind of medicine to encourage one's career. We must not indulge in it or let love run wild, so as to destroy one's career. Other things, like using bad methods to entice male colleagues to substitute for one's own work and not going to the office, are the worst kind of common behavior, and should also be corrected as soon as possible.

The Life of Joan of Arc, the French Heroine

— Ms. Cao Yi

The most famous woman in France that everyone knows is Madame Roland, but they forget about a woman who sacrificed herself to save her country in the fifteenth century, and that woman was Joan of Arc.

Arc was the daughter of a village farmer. As a child, after school, she would help her father work in the fields; at night, she would sit by her mother's side spinning cotton until late. There was a small grove of trees by her house, where the neighborhood children often gathered to jump, play, and sing, and Arc sometimes joined them. Even the birds and beasts in the woods were her good friends; the little sparrows were not afraid of her and always came to perch on her shoulders. It is said that she could even summon wild animals to play. In worldly terms, she was an innocent and carefree village girl. She loved listening to the bells of the church and also liked to serve the sick in her village.

In 1429, she was already eighteen years old. At that time, King Charles of France was under attack by the English, and the French troops were retreating day by day, while the English army was advancing inch by inch, and the whole country was terrified! In this critical moment, Arc was lying in bed one day when she suddenly saw a divine being appear to her, ordering her to go see the French king and restore the authority of France. She said, "I am just a farmer's daughter and do not know how to lead troops into battle." The divine being said, "God will help you." Arc then went to see King Charles and said, "God has commanded me to tell you that you will surely restore your authority and become God's general, ruling France." The king cheered and said, "God has sent you! Please lead my army to kill the enemy!" Arc led the troops onto the battlefield, wearing snow-white armor, holding a French lily in her hand, and was extremely brave. She was very tall and rode a horse like a man; she did not eat anything all day on horseback and did not feel tired. She led tens of thousands of soldiers as a mother leads a child. When she arrived at the battlefield, she waved her hand and shouted loudly, "Kill the enemy! Do not be afraid!" When the soldiers heard these words, their courage increased instantly, and they charged forward, defeating the enemy greatly. The enemy retreated into the fortress, and Arc led the soldiers to attack the fortress. Suddenly, she was injured and fell to the ground, and the soldiers lost their morale and prepared to retreat. Arc suddenly got up! Shouting, "Wait! Rest for a while! If you see my flag touching the enemy's wall, then attack bravely!" As a result, they won a great victory. After reaching the castle, she ran to the church to thank God.

After the war was over, her great task was accomplished. Arc asked the king to let her go home, but the king refused. At this time, the English, having been defeated greatly, were determined to seek revenge. Arc continued to fight bravely, but unfortunately, she was captured by a villain named Bastar. He sold her to the English, who regarded her as a sorceress and locked her in prison for a whole year. Later, they falsely accused her of being a witch and sentenced her to death. Then, they brought her to the middle of the street, tied her with a thick rope, and piled firewood underneath. Arc calmly raised her head to the sky and cried out loudly, "English! English! I am afraid that in the future you will suffer endless pain because of my death!" Before the cry had ended, a fierce fire blazed up.

Ms. Arc died! She sacrificed herself for the country! She awakened the hot blood of all the French people! She restored the land of France!

The current situation in China is probably more dangerous than France in the fifteenth century, but the women of China have completely forgotten the spirit of courage of Ms. Arc and are still living their comfortable lives in a drunken stupor. My dear sisters! Our end is near! Wake up! Follow the spirit of Ms. Arc and save our endangered country!

Special Article in this Newspaper

Impressionistic Notes on the Three Heroines of Lingnan, Xiong Bishuang, Yaoshuang, and Peishuang, Sisters of Shining Talents and Paired Pendants

— Jiping

Science can save the country, and art can also save the country; since we are Chinese, we should serve China!

The three Lingnan Xiong sisters, Bishuang, Yaoshuang, and Peishuang, are renowned in the art world. Fortunately, they have been praised by important figures in the party and government, which has increased their reputation tenfold. Originally, in the current stage, no matter what academic expert you are, you will not be able to increase your status by relying on your own strength. Unless you have the support of prominent figures, you will never be able to show your face. Art is originally the noblest and most detached thing. I wonder how many artists nowadays have become famous by their own skills? How many are not specially promoted by distinguished and powerful figures? In other words, artistic achievement must have considerable skill to enjoy considerable fame. This is as it should be. We naturally dare not compliment those who have mediocre skills but possess false reputations. Like the two Lingnan heroines, who went to Beijing last year at the behest of Mr. Wang Jingwei to exhibit their works, I think those who have not seen them will inevitably have doubts about their art. This is human nature and not surprising. The day before yesterday, the three sisters came to Shanghai together. Driven by curiosity, I went to visit them. First, I viewed their works, including flowers, birds, figures, individual and collaborative pieces. After appreciating more than a dozen new works, I was convinced that their skills were profound and extraordinary. They truly captured the essence of Yun Shouping's style. With such young ages and such good achievements, it is no coincidence that they can gain the appreciation of important figures.

They are originally from Panyu. Their father was a Qing dynasty scholar and a student of Mr. Yu Quyuan. The Xiong family has five daughters and three sons. Bishuang is the second daughter. When she and her two younger sisters were studying at Zhixin Girls' School in Guangzhou, Wang Jingwei taught literature courses, and Sun Zhesheng and Zhu Jiahua were school board members, so they had a deep teacher-student relationship. Later, they entered the Faculty of Arts at the University of Hong Kong and graduated together last summer. The three sisters initially learned Western painting and later switched to Chinese painting, under the guidance of Gao Qifeng, Rong Zhongsheng, and Zhang Zichu. Over the past ten years, their art has greatly improved. They went to the capital last year and held an exhibition. In May of this year, they held a pre-departure exhibition. In these few days, they will hold another pre-departure exhibition in Shanghai. The location and date will be determined by the municipal government. After the exhibition, they will return to Guangdong and set off overseas, first to Singapore and other major ports in Southeast Asia to exhibit their works, and then directly to Germany, followed by England and France. Next year, they will visit the United States, travel back to China via Japan, for a period of one year. This time, they are under the order of the Ministry of Education to investigate the art of European and American countries, and incidentally exhibit their works to promote Chinese art abroad, while also hoping to absorb more Western painting styles and techniques.

"After investigating Europe and America and returning to China, how will you work hard for your future?" I asked.

"Our plan is to return to Guangdong after returning to China to establish a women's art college to cultivate new talents. Currently, Guangzhou only has a municipal art vocational school, and there is no such school specifically for women in the country. Many people in the central government have expressed sympathy. This time, we will first make preliminary contacts with the provincial and municipal authorities in Guangdong. Besides this, there is no second plan."

"Do you three sisters have the same aspirations?"

Shuangtuo said, "Yes! The three of us have the same knowledge, the same interests, and the same goals, of course."

"In that case, you are truly three in one." So everyone laughed for a while.

"Just as you are going abroad, the national crisis is becoming increasingly tense. May I ask what you think about this?"

Peishuang said: "We are too young and only know how to paint a few strokes. How dare we talk about national affairs. However, art can represent the nation's characteristics. Science can save the country, and art can also save the country, but the methods are slightly different. Since the 'September 18th' Incident, we have also had many works that express patriotism, such as 'Wagtails in the Meadow', 'Birds Singing in Tall Trees', 'Geese Coming to Fruition'... all of which are lyrical works about the national crisis and have attracted everyone's attention."

"What opinions do you three sisters usually have on women's issues?"

All three of them had opinions on this issue. Later, Bishuang summarized them and said again: "Women account for at least half of the entire nation. Since we are all Chinese, we should equally shoulder the responsibility of saving China. How can we save the country? This cannot be summed up in a few words. As for the three of us, we can only start with ourselves, train our talents, and enrich our knowledge; standing in the position of art creators, we must take on the responsibility of saving the country in our respective positions. In addition to investigating art on this trip, we will pay attention to the strengths of women in various countries and bring them back for our female compatriots to refer to.

As we were talking, someone pushed open the door and entered the room, shook hands as a greeting, and said to the reporter: "...Although my daughters have lived in Hong Kong and Guangdong for a long time and traveled far to Beijing and Shanghai, and have graduated from university, they still have not been infected with the habits of the city and can maintain a loyal and sincere attitude, which is enough to comfort us. Now that they have returned to the prosperous city, they are originally ignorant and simply like country people visiting the City God Temple, and they all need the guidance of senior gentlemen. In addition to studying and painting, they do not ask about foreign affairs and do not understand socializing. This time abroad gives them the opportunity to know the new trends in Eastern and Western cultural undertakings..."

The three sisters of the same mind, sent to study abroad, traveling in Europe and America, investigating art, is indeed a glorious page in the history of the Chinese women's movement. However, the customs of Western countries are somewhat different from those of our country, such as the etiquette of social engagements, the healthy and lively nature, especially for women, should be paid attention to; the artistic works of the Xiong sisters have reached the top, but they still retain the gentle breath of ladies, and when they see people, they seem shy and timid, and their bodies seem thin. In the eyes of Westerners, they may misunderstand that Chinese women still have this sickly beauty.

The Three Xiong Sisters and Their Signatures

Biographies of Famous Women in the World (5)

— Lusha Bai

The most outstanding female politician in the Soviet Union today is Yelena Dmitriyevna Stasova. Since the decline of Kollontai and Krupskaya, and before Nikolayeva and Kaluykina emerged, she has been engaged in the revolutionary struggle for thirty-six years and is now the chairman of the International Relief Organization, with a high reputation internationally.

In the thirty-six years of struggle, from Lenin to Stalin, she occupied almost half of the party history of the Soviet Union. From the time of the founding of "Iskra" at the end of the nineteenth century, she often participated in all the secrets of the party. Among the veterans of the Soviet revolution, she can be considered one of the few.

Stasov

She looks like a typical female weaver, extremely serious and enthusiastic about her career. Work is her life. Unlike ordinary politicians who use public office for private gain, she has never been involved in political relations because of emotional factors. No matter what her political tendencies, she can always adapt to the trend and be loyal to her duties.

During the first revolutionary struggle, she was arrested at the Novgorod station and imprisoned in the Moscow Taganskaya Prison. During the second revolution, she was sentenced to exile and later escaped to St. Petersburg, where she organized the Central Party Department with Molotov and others, and invited Ilyich to preside over it. After the success of the revolution, she was elected as an alternate member of the Central Committee at the Sixth Party Congress, and as a member of the Central Committee at the Seventh and Eighth Party Congresses. In 1920, she was appointed as a guide at the First Oriental National Congress held in Baku. In 1933, she served as a member of the purge committee during the party purge. She is currently the chairman of the International Relief Organization, and has been in office for six years, constantly fighting against the white terror around the world, enthusiastically helping oppressed people around the world. Last year, on the occasion of her sixtieth birthday, the entire Soviet Union warmly congratulated her.

Women's Family Pastimes

— Zhiyun

The Columbia Women's Club of Vancouver, Canada, has been established for more than ten years and has nearly four thousand members. The club not only has well-equipped clubhouses to provide members with the convenience of life, as well as physical and moral cultivation, but also focuses on the design of general women's family life. In the spring of this year, the club hired twelve experts who have long studied women's family life to engage in research suitable for general women's family life. The twelve experts include three Canadians, three Americans, four from the United Kingdom and other territories, one overseas Chinese student in the United States, and one French person. After four months of careful discussion and exchange of opinions, the following items were unanimously recognized as the most suitable family pastimes for women in their spare time or after taking care of household chores.

(1) Knitting with wool and cotton yarn, such as hats, shawls, coats, tablecloths, etc.

(2) Embroidery, such as all kinds of patterns on clothes, shoes and hats, as well as embroidery on curtains, sofa cushions, tablecloths, gloves, etc.

(3) Planting flowers. The vacant land in the garden next to the house can be used as a good place for planting flowers. Water and cultivate them every day so that when the flowers bloom, they can be used as altar offerings for the family.

(4) Arranging the furniture and sundries in the home to make it beautiful and clean.

(5) Raising domestic animals and poultry to increase the vitality of the family.

(6) Promoting indoor sports, such as flexibility exercises and table tennis, so that every woman has a certain amount of exercise every day, which can not only improve health, but also regulate the circulation of blood solution in the human body and make the appearance beautiful.

Regarding items (1) and (2), the club will further invite several knitting and embroidery experts to compile textbooks for a long time and draw all kinds of new design patterns, publish them in special books, or in the club's publications, and in several women's magazines in Canada and the United States, for general women to use. For items (3) and (5), the club will also hire several experts to write articles and introduce all kinds of flowers, grasses, trees, and trees suitable for foreign language families to plant, as well as poultry, fish, birds, and beasts suitable for family raising. Club members have the opportunity to obtain free written or face-to-face inquiries. It is expected that after one year, if the results are excellent, the eastern part of the club intends to expand and hire several family instructors to be used by members to invite to their homes for guidance. In addition to compiling and printing pamphlets to guide general women with the knowledge and principles of arrangement and tidiness, item (5) also plans to hire three or four experts to give periodic public lectures and provide consultations for members. For item (6), in addition to writing promotion, it also plans to compile and print wall charts, and shoot slides and moving films to promote to members. Regarding the above six items, the club provides all the tools, raw materials, and seeds, etc., except for a portion for members to purchase, and at the same time, it specially appoints several related stores to sell them to the club at a considerable value for convenience.

In addition to the above six items, the twelve research members have also designed several outdoor pastimes, such as (1) travel during holidays, (2) boating, (3) driving a car, (4) riding a bicycle, (5) photography..., etc. Because of the limited space and because women in our country have not yet reached a considerable level, they are omitted. —Regarding these outdoor activities, the club will also hire several responsible instructors to provide members with various conveniences.

Women in our country have no entertainment in their families. All spare time, or the remaining moments of handling housework, are almost completely consumed in a decadent life. On the one hand, it is said that it does not allow the cultivation of temperament and virtue, and on the other hand, it cannot be said to be beneficial to health or seek interest. Women who live in this decadent life, in addition to developing a grumpy temper and a narrow self, which breaks the joy of the family, there is really no better result that can be produced. Therefore, here I especially introduce some experts' family life design plans to the readers. I hope that the women's world in our country will quickly jump out of the decadent life and pursue a rational family life.

The Eldest Sister I Haven't Seen in Ten Years (Part 1)

— Li Shouzhen

When I returned home this summer vacation, I accidentally ran into Ping's eldest sister. If she hadn't recognized me and excitedly called out my nickname, her haggard face and her untimely dress almost made me completely unable to recognize who she was. How would I have thought that my eldest sister, who was so beautiful, delicate, and very neat, would change into this appearance in less than ten years!

When I saw that it was her, I ran to her immediately. She still grabbed my hand as enthusiastically as before and asked about my situation in the past few years. So I told her that after graduating from junior high school in this county, I went to Shanghai to attend high school, and then went on to university. Now I have graduated from university and am working. After listening to my words, she sighed with infinite emotion and said, "Oh, you children are all making progress. Ping is also in Shanghai now. You can go see her when you have time! Her life is not as good as yours. She often writes to complain about her loneliness and mental discomfort. Now she is the mother of two children. Although the life of a small family is still happy, she has no career or future of her own, so she is always very empty. You used to be such a good pair. Now you are going your separate ways." As she spoke, infinite repression was revealed in her two big eyes that had been praised by many people. Finally, she told me Ping's address in Shanghai and said that her child at home was sick, so she left hurriedly.

As her back disappeared from my eyes like autumn leaves, I suddenly felt lost!

It was only ten years ago, right? At that time, I was only thirteen years old and studying in a local junior high school. Ping and I were classmates in elementary school. We were not only the same age, but also had similar figures and personalities. People who didn't know us always thought we were sisters, and we had always been as close as sisters. At that time, Ping's eldest sister taught at the elementary school attached to our school. She not only had very good teaching methods and was very good at Chinese, but she also had a special talent for music and handicrafts. Moreover, she was young, beautiful, lively, and kind, so the local society recognized her as a typical new woman. In school, her long singing voice and gentle personality made every elementary school student surround her, and her unique kindness and generosity made even the workers in the school very grateful to her.

Every winter, Ping always wore her new wool sweater and new gloves, and ran to school happily, boasting about her eldest sister's love for her. And in the summer, her eldest sister would make her the most fashionable lapel short shirt at that time. The classmates were very envious of her, and my eldest sister would always send me a pair of gloves or a scarf every year, so I was also happier than other classmates.

However, old etiquette and social habits did not allow a girl who was over twenty years old to stay with her mother. Ping's eldest sister was already a girl over twenty years old, so her parents began to worry, because they could not find a good son-in-law for this perfect daughter, so they were worried. So they sent out news of choosing a son-in-law everywhere, and unmarried men everywhere wanted to court this good match. Finally, one morning, Ping ran to tell me with a face full of smiles that her parents had obtained the consent of her eldest sister and had engaged her.

That year's winter vacation, I returned to the countryside and waited until school started. When I met Ping, the first thing she said was that her eldest sister had already gotten married. And she had resigned from her teaching position at the attached elementary school and was preparing to go to Shanghai with her husband. From then on, I never saw my eldest sister again, and Ping rarely mentioned her news, until later Ping got married and we lost contact.

Findings from Interviews with Professional Women: (2) Thoughts and Lives of Female Employees at the New Asia Hotel

— Xianying

There are further similarities, namely:

(1) They can all represent upright and noble women from middle-class families.

(2) In terms of knowledge, they all have the qualifications of a junior high school graduate or one year lower or higher who has received civic education.

(3) They have no bad habits, let alone vulgar and absurd behaviors. They are very responsible at work, very satisfied with their positions, and good citizens who can love and respect themselves.

In addition to the above six similarities, I would also like to write a special feature on individuals: Mary—a Chinese-Western mixed-style girl from Ningxin, with a short stature and full of energy. Compared to the tragic star Sylvia Sidney, she is not lying. She studied in a foreign school since she was a child, speaks impeccable English, and is lively and fluent in her answers.

Yuping—the most knowledgeable among her colleagues, having worked as a teacher and writing beautiful calligraphy. She likes sports and filled the role as the captain of the school basketball team, once she stood out. She is very naive, has a special posture when walking, and has an egg-shaped face and medium stature. She likes to learn to fly an airplane, and she told people that it was a pity that she didn't have the opportunity.

Peiyi—is a child, but the oldest in age. She likes to swim, her tongue is too short, her pronunciation is inaccurate, but she is very hardworking and is taking English lessons.

Xiuzhen—a female social activist, her compassionate heart is as developed as her fat body. She has lost money running a civilian night school, and is now also the director of nursing education. She wears cloth clothes and cloth shoes, and firmly believes in Christianity.

Xiuqin—is the youngest, but very capable. She can drive an elevator and also be a chef. She can speak Suzhou dialect and Shanghai dialect. In particular, her ability to be thrifty is even more outstanding. It is said that she is reluctant to spend two dimes on a movie.

According to all their similarities, they can very well represent the majority of modern professional women—middle class, average knowledge, twenty-something, forty or fifty yuan a month. Therefore, I believe that my interviews with only five of them can very well tell the various aspects of the lives and thoughts of professional women. Below, I list seven major questions and let's see the answers they gave me.

Supplement to the Local Section of Shen Bao

Spiritual Pivot and Plain Questions

— Doctor Liu Xinbai's main answers

Important Information for Seeking Medical Advice (Issue 4)

1. Letters should be written in vernacular Chinese.

2. Do not use vague terms like "wind," "cold," "fire," or "dampness" to describe illnesses, nor should you use ambiguous "disease names" that lack specific meaning.

3. Describe your symptoms in as much detail as possible.

4. Please include postage stamps with your letters: five cents for out-of-town mail, two cents for local mail. We reserve the right to reply directly to letters without publishing them if we deem them lacking in public value or if the patient prefers confidentiality.

5. Please clearly write your detailed address.

6. Send letters to my clinic: No. 1108, Qinyuan Village, Xinzha Road, Shanghai.

7. Medical consultations are free of charge.

8. If you are asking about two different illnesses in one letter, or several aspects of one illness – such as its causes, symptoms, diagnosis, prognosis, and treatment – please number them accordingly.

9. Medical advice is limited to internal medicine and dermatology/venereology.

10. This column will publish answers publicly every Saturday.

Blood in Semen

###

Number 30, Mr. Chen Rongquan of No. 81, Yongyu Lane, Ximen Road asks: I was enticed by bad friends to visit a prostitute once, resulting in profuse white discharge and extreme pain. After reading in the newspaper about "Nemesis of Syphilis" treating gonorrhea, I bought and took it, and the discharge did indeed seem to be completely cured! Recently, I accidentally read some lewd books and performed self-stimulation, resulting in blood mixed in the semen, with a reddish-brown color. There are no other symptoms. (1) What disease is this? (2) What treatment method should I use and what medicines should I take? (3) Will this be harmful to my body in the future?

Answer: (1) It is "seminal vesiculitis." (2) Massage, cold water baths, and injections of "Guoneng Kelin" (Sino-Acrindin) and "Xinya Calcium" (Sinocalcin). Other than cold water baths, these require a doctor to administer. (3) It will cause problems with fertility.

Swollen Legs

###

Number 21, Mr. Xia Anzhi asks: I am 18 years old. I quit school to go into business at the age of sixteen, so I lack exercise and receive little sunlight. My development is otherwise complete, and my body is quite tall. At the end of the year before last, while washing my feet, I noticed slight swelling in the depressions of my ankles, but I didn't pay attention to it. Last spring, I suddenly felt even more swelling, so I bought five boxes of foot swelling pills from the OOO Pharmacy in Dainanmen, but they had no effect. Then I went to a Chinese medicine doctor, OOO, for injections, but this also failed to remove the swelling. I heard it was caused by kidney deficiency, and that eating turtles could reduce swelling, so I ate four or five of them, but there was no change. This spring, I read in a book that it was caused by a lack of "Vitamin B," so I bought rice bran from the grain store and ate it, which seemed to reduce the swelling quite a bit. Now, I would like to ask: (1) What is the actual cause of this disease? (2) What kind of medicine can completely remove it? (3) Please indicate which methods of health maintenance are necessary, indicating surgery(?). (4) I have a lot of phlegm; what medicine can I take to remove this?

(1) Two diseases can cause these symptoms: beriberi and cardiac edema. What you have can only be determined after an examination. The cause of beriberi is a lack of "Vitamin B1," along with bacterial infection. (2) Please have a doctor inject "Tui E Shui" (Theosal), which can completely eliminate the swelling, but if it is beriberi, it is essential to also take "Vitamin B" (Vitamin-B). (3) Walk less, rest more, and do not eat rice, but instead focus on eating noodles and vegetables. Since eating bran is effective, you might as well continue to eat it. (4) Take "Baikeding" (Pacdin) tablets, three times a day, two tablets each time.

Blood in Phlegm

###

Number 32, Mr. Huang Shixi of No. 13, Xiushui Beach, Xiaonanmen Wai, Nanshi asks: I am twenty-one years old this year. In mid-May of last year, I suddenly had a small amount of red blood in my phlegm, but it has not happened since. I often feel dizzy and weak. In June, my throat suddenly became hoarse, and my voice is now completely gone, with all medicines proving ineffective. In September, after an X-ray, I finally learned that I have lung disease. May I ask: (1) Is the loss of voice related to lung disease? If so, what is the reason? (2) Is there any hope of regaining my voice? (3) What is the appropriate treatment, and what medicines should I take regularly?

Answer: (1) The loss of voice is due to laryngeal tuberculosis. The medical term for lung pain is "pulmonary tuberculosis." The close relationship between the two is self-evident. (2) It is difficult to expect a full recovery without proper treatment. (3) Drug therapy: injections of "Gaigushen" (Calchosen), oral "Xinya Calcium" (Sinocalcin) tablets, and "Yuya Calcium." Nutritional therapy: eat what you like. Sunlight therapy: bask your chest in the morning sunlight for twenty minutes each day. Pneumothorax.

Lead Poisoning Abdominal Pain

###

Number 33, Mr. Cheng Yinrui of Minsheng Printing House, Avenue Edward VII asks: I am twenty-three years old. I have been working at this printing house as a typesetter for four years. Less than half a year after starting, I began to have frequent stomach pains, as sharp and stabbing as if something was being twisted inside. It feels like there is a hard lump below my navel. When the pain strikes, I feel dizzy, my face turns as white as paper, and beads of sweat roll down my body like raindrops. Therefore, I ask (1) What is this disease? (2) Can the doctor cure it? (3) What is the treatment? (4) Is it appendicitis?

Answer: (1) "Chronic lead poisoning," also known as "lead colic." This is because you unknowingly inhaled lead dust, which accumulated over time and is now causing trouble in your body. Typesetters are prone to this disease. (2) You don't necessarily need to consult me. Any qualified modern doctor can treat this disease with great confidence. (3) An injection of 5% "calcium chloride" can immediately relieve the pain, and a few injections can cure it completely. (4) No.

Page 21

Commentary

The Problem of Reducing the Number of Rickshaws

— Jianping

Rickshaws are truly having a very unlucky time these days. Not long ago, to restrict the increase in the number of public rickshaws and limit the number of rickshaw registration quotas, one disaster after another fell upon their heads, making it impossible for them to maintain even the most basic living despite their blood and sweat. Now, their unprecedented crisis has arrived: the suggestion by the Concession authorities to reduce the number of rickshaws. This problem quickly spread, and even the rickshaw owners felt threatened and uneasy.

Originally, under the so-called wave of economic recession, layoffs and salary reductions are very common. Therefore, some people think that reducing the number of rickshaws is just another form of cutting back in the rickshaw industry, and they treat it as something very ordinary. We believe that this view of the problem is inappropriate. Without even mentioning whether it has anything in common with layoffs and salary reductions, the starting point for reducing the number of rickshaws is that people in modern civilization feel that rickshaws are backward and "inhumane." This principle of abolishing rickshaws makes us feel that it cannot be equated with the former. This is "elimination," not simply due to the economic downturn in the rickshaw industry.

Now, let's discuss the question of whether this "elimination" is an appropriate method. Of course, in this era of the 20th century with its highly developed mechanical industry, it is not surprising to advocate the elimination of this "inhumane," old system of one person driving another. However, if we simply feel that it is "unacceptable" and then try to completely eliminate rickshaws by starting with "reduction" and "restriction," this is not very appropriate. In the past, during rickshaw-related disputes, such as the dispute over restricting registration, such as preparing rickshaw coolie benefit associations, etc., I have said that if we want to completely resolve the rickshaw pullers' problems, we should start by solving their livelihoods. Therefore, the "biggest reason" for the several rickshaw pullers' disturbances "is that the suffering of the rickshaw pullers themselves has not been noticed." Now, we have seen the news of the rickshaw pullers staging a major petition to the Municipal Council. The main points of their petition are nothing more than: (1) reorganize the rickshaw pullers' mutual aid association; (2) abolish restrictions on rickshaw pullers' registration; (3) drop the proposal to reduce the number of rickshaws. From this, we see that although the current rickshaw pullers' problems can be considered to have come to an end for the time being, they have not been thoroughly resolved after all. The problems still exist and are still just as serious. The problem of reducing the number of rickshaws is simply a continuation of the previous problems, and this time even the interests of the rickshaw owners have been affected, making the problem even more complex.

Recently, we have not seen any results regarding this issue. However, we have a very small hope. That is to ask those who advocate for the complete abolition of rickshaws to pay some attention to what will happen to the livelihoods of the tens of thousands of rickshaw pullers who will be abolished. Of course, their current inhumane lives should be rescued, but the method of rescue is definitely not to abolish them and expect a good outcome. Abolishing rickshaws will undoubtedly cause them to lose their jobs. At that time, their lives will not even be comparable to "inhumane lives." Therefore, we very much hope that this time the problem of reducing the number of rickshaws will have a very thorough solution.

Talking About Tour Guides

— Shih Huaizi

In American movies, there are quite a few films that feature tour guides as the main characters (I remember "The Moon and Sixpence"). The ending is always the same as in general American romance movies: the male tour guide gets a beautiful and affectionate (sometimes even wealthy) wife. In China, the situation seems somewhat different. Although tour guide agencies are now booming, there are no male tour guides – or perhaps there are? But I have never seen them in advertisements. Even if there were, I don't think anyone would hire them. As for female tour guides, those who hire them to "guide" are mostly foreign firm employees who have lived in Shanghai for a long time, small clerks in various organizations, and university students who ask them to "guide" things like how to eat steamed buns (see the confession of a female tour guide in the Da Wan Bao). It's as if these people have never eaten steamed buns in their lives.

At first, I didn't quite understand the reason for this. I just thought that the reason why the tour guide industry is so developed is probably because Shanghai is a major commercial port that is the focus of attention for both China and foreign countries. But after learning that so-called tour guides even have to guide people on how to eat steamed buns, I thought that the reason why the tour guide industry is so developed is that they also have to work as "nannies" in addition to "tour guides."

But this "assumption" that I thought was close to correct was broken by the classified ads in the newspapers. One company said in an advertisement, "Lonely nights are long; accompany you to dispel worries and relieve boredom." Another said, "Where can you find beauties of national charm? Search for charming faces here." They probably feared that people wouldn't believe them, so they even printed photos of "charming faces" to show their sincerity. As for those who advertise under the name of "generosity" or who call for customers by saying that "beautiful female staff members will personally distribute stimulating and exciting souvenirs to all," that is even more common and nothing special.

To have tour guides use "national charm" and "charming faces" to attract customers, the reason for this is already profound enough, not to mention the stimulating and exciting souvenirs. But if you use "Lonely nights are long; accompany you to dispel worries and relieve boredom" as an annotation for "tour guide," it is probably not entirely wrong.

Because they "accompany you to dispel worries and relieve boredom," in addition to "charming faces," understanding and catering to the "customer's psychology" naturally becomes an even more important condition. So one company's advertisement said, "We have experts to train our staff in how to respond to customers," "We have experts to manage our staff's makeup," "We have experts to study customer psychology." With so many "experts" training them, the "staff members" who come out for interviews are naturally ones that "the customer loves and is reluctant to let go."

In this difficult era, ordinary citizens need a little "stimulation" to numb their souls. It is no longer something that can be changed by simply scolding them. And they understand that everything needs a beautiful coat to serve as a talisman. Although the road hidden by the beautiful coat is a road to depravity, this road to depravity is supported by life. Therefore, high-sounding terms like "public morals" have no effect on it. At most, the beautiful coat is torn and replaced with another, but the core remains the same, and may even be more terrifying.

Therefore, what I am worried about is not the weeping and wailing of moralists, but that this pathological phenomenon will not last long. At that time, the ordinary citizens who seek stimulation to numb their souls will no longer have the strength to do so. So there is no need to scold them anymore. All the beautiful coats will have lost their power of seduction, and the day of total collapse will have arrived.

Although I am afraid to see such a phenomenon, I hope it will come, because I know that it will come sooner or later, and no force can stop it.

And behind the decay, new light will use these corpses as fertilizer to bloom brilliant flowers.

Child (Continued)

— Xiu Yang

I was educating my child in that way.

But in early spring this year, my child fell seriously ill. For the first time, I paid twenty-four yuan for a doctor to prescribe medicine. The child was sick for two months, and the medical expenses took away four months of my salary. My mother prayed every day in front of the Guanyin statue, willing to make any sacrifice as long as the child got better. But I still felt that the sacrifice was too great. On the night when the child was in the most danger, my mother unintentionally said that he was a debt owed from a previous life, so he came to "collect a debt." Having a child is "repaying a debt." This statement has a profound meaning, at least in my personal opinion.

The child got better, and by the time he recovered and got out of bed, he had almost completely changed, although he still retained his uniquely stubborn personality. He gave up everything that children liked. He was no longer a "philanthropist" or a "fun-loving child." He was silent and rarely smiled, like adults who have encountered unpleasant things. A six-year-old child resembled a sixty-year-old man. I was very unhappy with his behavior, and I tried even harder to restore his innocence, but it was no use. Until now, my mother still says that he has a "noble appearance" and that "he will definitely have good fortune in the future after surviving a great disaster."

My education has failed!

While the child was sick, my wife became pregnant again. My mother was naturally very happy. She calculated the time of delivery and used various "fortune-telling" methods to guess whether the future little life would be a boy or a girl. Mothers of the same age as my mother, because my eldest child "survived a great disaster" and now there is the joy of another child this year, often discussed "children" and "good fortune" with laughter.

Before my wife gave birth, one day under the lamp, my mother suddenly asked me whether I preferred to have a boy or a girl. Since the child came to "collect a debt," then it didn't matter whether it was a boy or a girl. I answered my mother frankly that it was good to have either. But my mother asked me with a joyful heart, and I, as my mother's "debt-collecting" child, should naturally guess whether she preferred to have a boy or a girl first. So I answered her like this:

"It is naturally better to have a boy, but there should also be a girl."

This answer exactly matched my mother's intention, although she knew that this was the slipperiest answer. The whole family waited for my wife's labor in joy.

The night before yesterday, my wife went into labor and gave birth to a boy, but he died after three minutes. This made my mother somewhat unhappy. She naturally treasured her eldest grandson, who "will definitely have good fortune in the future," even more.

I felt as if my wife had never been pregnant or given birth to a child. I had "repaid" a "debt" and felt an unparalleled relief. But looking at my eldest child, who was still so "precocious," I became sad again. I didn't know how to educate this "creditor."

Although my mother liked that silent and rarely smiling "noble appearance."

Page 22

On the Provincial Highway

— Youqi

—Miscellaneous Thoughts

Carrying an uneasy heart, rushing out from Black Tooth's ambush by the wolf pack, at least, one can say that it was supreme luck. However, one cannot let that make one's heart calm down. Thinking of that place not far away -- said to have the same perilousness as Jiupanzi -- one cannot stop one's heart from leaping. I wondered what kind of scene it would be, my thoughts tinged with a bit of leniency --

-- Perhaps, late at night, it won't be as terrifying as they say?

Listening to the wheels grinding against the broken road surface, listening to the echoes of the wind from the valley: the moonlight thinly veiled the floating clouds, the mountains and fields still held a chaotic outline. Judging by the rate of speed, we had traveled about five miles from where we started. As for human traces? Humph, you couldn't even find the traces of ghosts.

After that, the driver spoke up again:

-- If a lone traveler walked this road at night, he'd be as good as dead! The meaning of the words, we all understood. However, he overlooked the fact that since the highway was already open to cars, why would a lone traveler need to travel the night road?

-- But there still have to be people traveling on this road! I added: Small merchants rushing to the market, aren't they still rushing along the long night road with the stars above their heads?

-- Naturally, but those goods aren't worth much money. For the sake of "knowing the local roads," they might be considered an extra boundary. Even if not, they can pull out the weapon from their chest, and a single spear can fight against a horse for quite a few rounds!

"Weapon"? "Fight"? My thoughts turned rapidly a few times, and I thought of the cloth bag that the porter was carrying on the mountain road, tightly wrapped around his waist. It seemed like there was something inside. At first, I always thought it was just packed with dry rations, but now I know that in addition to dry rations, there was also a "weapon" that could be used to "fight." Life originally takes different forms. In the mountainous countries that have not broken away from primitive life, there is also a way to adapt to themselves.

Because of this, the problem is solved: when they can "fight," they "fight." If they can't, they flee or even sacrifice themselves. If they encounter not people, but another group, the principle is also "the same."

As we walked, we gradually fell into a drowsy sleep again. Suddenly, after the entire car jolted twice, it stopped. The driver nudged Xiao Liu next to him, with a warning tone!

Be careful, ahead!

On the road five feet away, two people were sleeping soundly. To say they were sleeping, of course, wasn't accurate. Why were they lying in the middle of the road? Why in such a critical location? No need to say more, our nerves stimulated us to think in another direction. So, Ah Huang took out his weapon -- two people, easy to deal with, unless they don't come!

Finally, the two people got up, walked over slowly, bowing deeply, their faces gray. The turban on their heads had already rolled askew to one side. They looked like small merchants rushing to the market, but we couldn't see any carrying pole or frame.

-- Please, kind sirs, have pity on us! they said, their voices mournful. We are two brothers, preparing to go to the Black God Temple to rush to the market, but alas, the entire basket of salt cakes was taken away. After a pause, How can we explain it when we get home? We thought of Zazuo, or Xifeng, which is closer, to borrow some goods or money from relatives, but the journey is so long, our dry rations won't allow us to do that. We saw the lights from afar and lay down to seek saviors. Please, kind sirs, allow us to hitch a ride! Finally, they cried, their appearance very realistic.

We believed that it was definitely not oversensitivity. Someone with hidden intentions often uses various methods to achieve their ultimate goal. We certainly couldn't casually agree to this sudden event. Only after repeated questioning did we accept their request. Judging by the situation, even if they were really in disguise, it wouldn't matter; our weapons would be superior to their clumsy knives and guns.

After a while, the unpleasant thoughts dissolved. They were honest merchants who couldn't resist the fierce robberies even with iron rulers. Their hearts were sincere, and in such a short time, we became quite familiar. We shared the same indignation about their unfortunate robbery. Truly, it was a very bad year, and the place was barren. In their thoughts, they might think that our lives were in the so-called thirty-three heavens!

They got off at Zazuo.

Cow

— Er He

In June, I used the excuse of escaping the summer heat to sneak back to my hometown. I spent my days holed up in my room, fanning myself with a broken palm-leaf fan, wanting nothing more than to bury myself deep like a hibernating insect, hidden from everyone. But, perhaps because of my academic background, my relatives and friends in the countryside were curious and eager to engage with me. I thought that hiding away for too long wouldn't do, so like a weary migrating goose, I lonely returned to my old nest—Shanghai.

I intended to pick up my pen again and spend my life filling up the square grids of manuscript paper. But, unexpectedly, I received a letter from ×× Middle School, asking me to teach a few classes. The school was near the countryside, and for the sake of food and my health, I agreed without hesitation.

I had spent over ten years sitting on a bench listening to teachers lecturing with gestures. But standing on the podium myself to teach others was a first for me. Whether it was a first or not, I had to teach. So, I stood on the podium. After speaking for fifty minutes, the order was quite good, probably because I wore a pair of nearsighted glasses and my face always looked as somber as a cloudy day.

A cow just put to the plow is always fast, fast… it only wants to move forward and doesn't care whether the field is plowed straight or crooked. I am a cow just put to the plow. As I walked off the podium, I heard a student say, "This teacher speaks too fast and says too much." I walked straight to the lounge, feeling like golden flies were dancing before my eyes. I was too tired, like a tired cow just unhitched from the plow.

They have to attend classes for about 250 minutes each day, while I only teach for 100 minutes. But in terms of fatigue, I far surpass them. Besides attributing it to my poor health, I can only say that I am a cow just put to the plow!

What gives me the biggest headache is the heavy burden of grading papers. Over 130 student papers consume all my time. Jing Jun, my colleague in the same room, is also grading over 80 papers. We put our desks together, and all the desk space is completely taken up by the papers. Like the waves of an early morning tide, one batch goes away, and another batch comes. Saturdays are even worse. Diaries, large characters, small characters, five or six hundred books piled up like a small mountain. One careless move, and it will collapse. However, dealing with these many books depends on Sundays, which ordinary people must rest on.

Since I am a cow, I certainly have to work on Sundays. I grit my teeth, regardless of morning or night, holding a pen, with my head down, checking, circling, dotting, adding. Thus, my life vanishes in the piles of papers. Even the sadness that used to be close to me gradually leaves me. Under the blazing lights, I find even the time to drink a glass of plain water precious. As soon as I get into bed, I fall sound asleep. When I wake up, I go to the podium, burying my head in papers.

Is this life fortunate or unfortunate? Late at night, waking from a dream, I occasionally hear the rustling rain on the old ginkgo tree, which gives rise to melancholy and insomnia. I warn myself, I cannot keep wasting my life like this. Am I not becoming soulless? I am really like a cow, both stupid and dull. Besides a coarse meal, I have almost lost everything. I am already a machine. Apart from work, there is nothing else. Indeed, this exactly fits the conditions of a cow: docile, hardworking, enduring hardship… I shout, I am a cow.

Facing life head-on, all dreams vanish. But I am a good dreamer. I like to live in dreams, whether they are crimson, purple, gray, or even black… As long as they are dreams, I like to dream them. But at this moment, there are no dreams at all, which makes me quite sad.

What will be the result of living this kind of life for a hundred years? Jing Jun certainly feels this question too. But he says, perhaps to console himself, "Personally speaking, this is right. But you have to think about it, supposing we teach this generation of children well, and this generation of children teach another generation of children well, what will the effect be on social progress a hundred years later? We are great." He laughs confidently and cheerfully.

Upon closer thought, this makes a lot of sense. But I am still a big child who doesn't understand anything. How can I teach others well? Supposing I really have a little power to teach this generation of children well, I would rather lose all my dreams and be a cow, docile, hardworking, enduring hardship… I shout, I will always be a cow.

Children of Nature

Song from the Lianhua film "Go to Nature": Coral shore, surging waves, sea breeze strokes long willows; my home is deep among white clouds, green mountains reflect the evening glow. Skirts woven from grass, clothes made of leather, not afraid of wind and snow; capture tigers on land, slay dragons at sea, have the strength to defeat enemies. Cast nets early, plow the fields late, work by the setting sun. The superior wins, the inferior loses, hand in hand, go to nature.

Afterthoughts

Since Xinsheng Radio moved to the new address of the Zhengjia Muqiao Renfang Hotel, it has been actively arranging things. Now the antenna has been completed, and the broadcast room is also being painted. Broadcasting will begin soon.

Every Saturday afternoon at 4:00 PM, Mr. Zhang Yangzhang, a cartoonist from the Sino-Western Radio Station, hosts the "Weekly Cartoon Lecture." This week's topic is "Overview of Cartoon Brushstrokes." In addition, Mr. Zhang's carefully crafted masterpiece, "Sketch Cartoons," has now been published. The selling price only recovers the cost of 15 cents. Listeners of my cartoon seat who send letters to the radio station to purchase will have the author personally sign and send it as a souvenir.

Movie News

"Crossroads" to Begin Work

It is heard that Shen Xiling's "Crossroads" will soon be on the photography field The script of Shen Xiling has been dealt with for several months, recently photography on is of "Die Together Heart to Heart" Qingming Festival, both films can be completed in about ten days before and after "Crossroads" will then take over work It is said that "Crossroads" is a tragicomic drama that takes place between several unemployed young men and women on the streets of Shanghai, and the leading actors besides Zhao Dan are all new people. Those who love Shen Xiling's works can wait and see "Crossroads"

About "Wolf Mountain Bloodshed Record"

Fei Mu's recent work, "Wolf Mountain Bloodshed Record," is currently filming on location in Su Mountain. Actors such as Li Lili, Zhang Ji, Shang Guanwu, Han Langan, Hong Jingling, Lan Ping, Bai Lu, Liu Qiong, Yin Xiucen, etc., are all working in Su. It is heard that this trip will require staying in Su for half a month, and the huge cost will be about 10,000 gold.

The wolves borrowed from zoos in various places to shoot "Wolf Mountain Bloodshed Record," and a large number of hunters borrowed from various places, in addition to those who have already been set up in Shanghai for filming, there are also many who are transported to Su to shoot in the big natural scene.

"Wolf Mountain Bloodshed Record," because it depicts the life of hunters and the struggle between humans and beasts, is extremely complicated in production, but director Fei Mu is very courageous, so he can overcome various difficulties. It is generally expected that this film will cause a sensation when it is released. Whether in the form of performance or its ideology, it is enough to surprise people.

It is heard that after Fei Mu's "Wolf Mountain Bloodshed Record" is completed, he will direct a historical drama with rich nationalistic ideas.
